<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Overview</h2><a id="user-content-overview" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Overview" href="#overview"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Slidercontrol V2.1 is a fully self-contained motorized camera slider controller built around an Arduino Mega 2560. It drives a NEMA 17 stepper motor with planetary gearbox via an A4988 driver and provides a touchscreen UI on a 3.5" TFT shield. An optional ultrasonic sensor acts as an automatic end-stop, and a galvanically isolated camera trigger fires a Canon DSLR in sync with slider movement for timelapse sequences.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Project History - Fork of Mega-Testberichte.de</h3><a id="user-content-project-history---fork-of-mega-testberichtede" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Project History - Fork of Mega-Testberichte.de" href="#project-history---fork-of-mega-testberichtede"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">This project started as a close implementation of the <a href="https://www.mega-testberichte.de/artikel/kameraslider-motorisieren" rel="nofollow">Mega-Testberichte.de motorized slider guide</a> by Marco Kleine-Albers, which I recommend consulting alongside this documentation for build photos, a step-by-step walkthrough and additional context - it is the more visually complete reference.</p>
<p dir="auto">Over time the project diverged significantly in both hardware and software. Key reasons for branching off:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>MobaTools instead of AccelStepper:</strong> The original guide uses AccelStepper, which generates blocking code during motor movement. When the ultrasonic end-stop sensor was added to the system (which predates the camera trigger), non-blocking motor control became a hard requirement - the sonar loop must keep running while the motor moves. MobaTools, developed by MicroBahner as an Arduino library for model railroaders (MOdel BAhn), provides a fully non-blocking stepper implementation and is optimized for fine-grained, precise movement control - exactly what smooth camera slider travel requires. The library origins in model rail applications mean it handles slow, precise, repeatable motion particularly well.</li>
<li><strong>Planetary gearbox motor:</strong> The motor choice with integrated 1:14 gearbox changes the tuning, microstepping strategy and speed range significantly compared to a standard NEMA 17.</li>
<li><strong>Camera trigger system:</strong> An entirely new hardware and software subsystem not present in the original guide.</li>
<li><strong>Serial remote control:</strong> Added for computer-controlled timelapse sequences.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">The original guide remains the better starting point for someone new to the project. This documentation focuses on what has changed, the reasoning behind it, and the specifics of this particular build.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Tested Payloads</h3><a id="user-content-tested-payloads" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Tested Payloads" href="#tested-payloads"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The system has been tested with the following camera setups on a horizontal slider:</p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Setup</th>
<th>Approx. Weight</th>
<th>Result</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Canon EOS 7D + lens</td>
<td>~1.5 kg</td>
<td>Reliable at all speed settings</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Canon EOS 5D Mark IV + lens</td>
<td>~2.5 kg</td>
<td>Reliable at all speed settings</td>
</tr>
<tr>

<td>Moved without issues</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto">The Canon C400 test in particular is notable - a cinema camera fully rigged approaches the practical limits of the slider platform itself.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Theoretical Maximum Load</h4><a id="user-content-theoretical-maximum-load" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Theoretical Maximum Load" href="#theoretical-maximum-load"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The following is a rough estimate based on component datasheets. Real-world load capacity depends heavily on slider bearing condition, belt tension, incline angle and chosen speed.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Motor output torque (at gearbox output shaft):</strong></p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="T_out = T_motor × gear_ratio × efficiency
T_out = 0.52 Nm × 13.73 × 0.80 = ~5.7 Nm (theoretical peak)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>T_out = T_motor × gear_ratio × efficiency
T_out = 0.52 Nm × 13.73 × 0.80 = ~5.7 Nm (theoretical peak)
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The gearbox max permissible continuous torque is rated at <strong>3 Nm</strong>, which is the practical ceiling regardless of motor output.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Force available at belt/drive:</strong><br>
Assuming a typical belt pulley radius of ~10–15 mm:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="F = T / r = 3 Nm / 0.012 m = 250 N (~25 kg-equivalent)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>F = T / r = 3 Nm / 0.012 m = 250 N (~25 kg-equivalent)
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Real limiting factors (in order of likely constraint):</strong></p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li><strong>Slider rated payload</strong> - the iFootage Shark S1 is rated for approximately 8 kg. This is the most restrictive limit for horizontal use.</li>
<li><strong>Gearbox max continuous torque</strong> - 3 Nm (5 Nm momentary peak)</li>
<li><strong>Gearbox shaft max axial load</strong> - 50 N (~5 kg linear force along the shaft axis)</li>
<li><strong>A4988 current limit</strong> - set to ~1.18 A in this build (~70% of rated); higher current settings increase torque headroom but also heat</li>
</ol>
<p dir="auto">For horizontal use, the slider's own payload rating is the practical limit. The motor and gearbox have significant torque headroom for loads within that rating. Inclined or vertical use would require a separate calculation and is untested.</p>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto">These figures are theoretical estimates derived from component datasheets and standard engineering assumptions. They are not guaranteed values. Do not exceed the rated capacity of your slider platform.</p>
</blockquote>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">What This Project Does</h3><a id="user-content-what-this-project-does" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: What This Project Does" href="#what-this-project-does"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The controller moves a camera along a slider rail at configurable speed, distance and direction. Three operating modes are available:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Normal Run</strong> - moves the slider a set distance at a set speed, with optional return to start position</li>
<li><strong>Manual Run</strong> - continuous motor rotation for free-form positioning, start/stop via touchscreen</li>
<li><strong>Timelapse</strong> - divides the total travel into equal sub-steps, pauses at each position for a configurable delay, and optionally fires the camera shutter at every stop</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">All parameters (speed, distance, ramp, delay, subdivisions) are adjusted on the touchscreen. The controller can also be operated via serial commands over USB.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">What You Need</h3><a id="user-content-what-you-need" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: What You Need" href="#what-you-need"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Electronics</strong></p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Item</th>
<th>Notes</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Arduino Mega 2560 (or clone)</td>
<td>AZ-Delivery clone confirmed working</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>3.5" parallel TFT LCD shield, 480×320</td>
<td>MCUFRIEND_kbv-compatible</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>A4988 stepper driver breakout board</td>
<td>Check R_CS marking before use (see <a href="#33-stepper-motor-driver-a4988">3.3</a>)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>NEMA 17 stepper motor</td>
<td>17HS19-1684s-PG14 with 1:14 planetary gearbox used here</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>100 µF electrolytic capacitor</td>
<td>Motor supply decoupling, placed close to A4988</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>12V / 5A DC power supply</td>
<td>Motor supply</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>USB power bank or 5V supply</td>
<td>Arduino logic supply</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4N33 optocoupler + 390 Ω resistor</td>
<td>Camera trigger circuit (optional)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2.5 mm TRS female jack</td>
<td>Camera trigger output (optional)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2.5 mm male to Canon N3 female cable</td>
<td>Off-the-shelf adapter cable (optional)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>HC-SR04 ultrasonic sensor</td>
<td>End-stop safety (optional, mutually exclusive with camera trigger)</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Mechanical</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Camera slider with accessible drive shaft (e.g. Rollei / iFootage Shark S1)</li>
<li>3D-printed motor mount adapted to your slider model (see <a href="#11-project-base">1.1 Sources</a>)</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Tools</strong></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Soldering iron</li>
<li>Multimeter - required for A4988 current limit calibration</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Wiring Overview</h3><a id="user-content-wiring-overview" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Wiring Overview" href="#wiring-overview"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="USB Power Bank ──────────────────────── Arduino Mega 2560
                                               │
                         ┌─────────────────────┼──────────────────┐
                         │                     │                  │
                    TFT Shield            A4988 Driver        D47 / D49
                  (direct plug-in         VDD  ← 5V           Camera trigger
                   onto Mega headers)     GND  ← GND (logic)  or HC-SR04
                                          EN   ← D23
                                          STEP ← D25
                                          DIR  ← D27
                                               │
12V / 5A PSU ──── [100 µF] ──── VMOT          │
             └──────────────── GND (motor)    │
                                          1A / 1B / 2A / 2B
                                               │
                                         Stepper Motor"><pre class="notranslate"><code>USB Power Bank ──────────────────────── Arduino Mega 2560
                                               │
                         ┌─────────────────────┼──────────────────┐
                         │                     │                  │
                    TFT Shield            A4988 Driver        D47 / D49
                  (direct plug-in         VDD  ← 5V           Camera trigger
                   onto Mega headers)     GND  ← GND (logic)  or HC-SR04
                                          EN   ← D23
                                          STEP ← D25
                                          DIR  ← D27
                                               │
12V / 5A PSU ──── [100 µF] ──── VMOT          │
             └──────────────── GND (motor)    │
                                          1A / 1B / 2A / 2B
                                               │
                                         Stepper Motor
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The TFT shield plugs directly onto the Arduino Mega headers - no separate display wiring required. Motor, A4988 and power supply are wired as a separate circuit. The camera trigger is a standalone optocoupler circuit connected to D47 and GND.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Important:</strong> The Arduino (logic) and the motor driver (power) use separate ground connections that share a common reference point only at the DC jack. See <a href="#33-stepper-motor-driver-a4988">Ground Separation</a> for details.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Serial / USB Remote Control</h3><a id="user-content-serial--usb-remote-control" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Serial / USB Remote Control" href="#serial--usb-remote-control"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The controller can be operated remotely over USB via any serial terminal (e.g. Arduino Serial Monitor, PuTTY) at <strong>115200 baud</strong>.</p>
<p dir="auto">Commands are comma-separated strings terminated with a newline (<code>\n</code>). Each field can optionally carry a label prefix using a colon (<code>label:value</code>) - the parser strips everything up to and including the last colon, so both formats are accepted.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Command format:</strong></p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mode,speed,distance,ramp,time,steps"><pre class="notranslate"><code>mode,speed,distance,ramp,time,steps
</code></pre></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Index</th>
<th>Field</th>
<th>Description</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>0</td>
<td>mode</td>
<td><code>normal</code>, <code>timelapse</code>, or <code>rth</code> (case-insensitive)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1</td>
<td>speed</td>
<td>Motor speed (steps/s)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2</td>
<td>distance</td>
<td>Travel distance in steps</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>3</td>
<td>ramp</td>
<td>Ramp/acceleration length in steps</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4</td>
<td>time</td>
<td>Timelapse delay between stops in seconds</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>5</td>
<td>steps</td>
<td>Number of timelapse subdivisions (minimum 2)</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Examples:</strong></p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="normal,600,33000,0,0,2
timelapse,400,33000,0,30,10
rth,0,0,0,0,0"><pre class="notranslate"><code>normal,600,33000,0,0,2
timelapse,400,33000,0,30,10
rth,0,0,0,0,0
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Unused fields still need to be present as placeholders. For <code>rth</code>, all fields after index 0 are ignored. The controller responds with status messages over the same serial connection.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">1. Sources &amp; Libraries</h2><a id="user-content-1-sources--libraries" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 1. Sources &amp; Libraries" href="#1-sources--libraries"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">1.1 Project Base</h3><a id="user-content-11-project-base" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 1.1 Project Base" href="#11-project-base"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">This project is based on a guide by Marco Kleine-Albers (Mega-Testberichte.de) and was adapted and extended for use with Adafruit TFT and MobaTools by Gregor Urabl (gregorurabl.at), optimized for the Rollei/iFootage Shark S1 slider and a planetary-geared stepper motor.</p>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Schematic</h2><a id="user-content-schematic" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Schematic" href="#schematic"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://private-user-images.githubusercontent.com/240971327/559222116-05a1f284-e010-41c4-a1aa-6b4b2ab373f1.jpg?jwt=eyJ0eXAiOiJKV1QiLCJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJpc3MiOiJnaXRodWIuY29tIiwiYXVkIjoicmF3LmdpdGh1YnVzZXJjb250ZW50LmNvbSIsImtleSI6ImtleTUiLCJleHAiOjE3NzI5OTU0MjgsIm5iZiI6MTc3Mjk5NTEyOCwicGF0aCI6Ii8yNDA5NzEzMjcvNTU5MjIyMTE2LTA1YTFmMjg0LWUwMTAtNDFjNC1hMWFhLTZiNGIyYWIzNzNmMS5qcGc_WC1BbXotQWxnb3JpdGhtPUFXUzQtSE1BQy1TSEEyNTYmWC1BbXotQ3JlZGVudGlhbD1BS0lBVkNPRFlMU0E1M1BRSzRaQSUyRjIwMjYwMzA4JTJGdXMtZWFzdC0xJTJGczMlMkZhd3M0X3JlcXVlc3QmWC1BbXotRGF0ZT0yMDI2MDMwOFQxODM4NDhaJlgtQW16LUV4cGlyZXM9MzAwJlgtQW16LVNpZ25hdHVyZT1lZTVlMTJiNWM4ZTBkNjRjZDNiZWIwODdkYWE1NjFlN2UxOTRhNWFjNGQ2MjE2NjkxZWViMTY4MmUxZGUyNDQ4JlgtQW16LVNpZ25lZEhlYWRlcnM9aG9zdCJ9.vxc0c4NMs5J7CEESs0bzGiJoipdTOYT78BsUHLCX7pw"><img src="https://private-user-images.githubusercontent.com/240971327/559222116-05a1f284-e010-41c4-a1aa-6b4b2ab373f1.jpg?jwt=eyJ0eXAiOiJKV1QiLCJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJpc3MiOiJnaXRodWIuY29tIiwiYXVkIjoicmF3LmdpdGh1YnVzZXJjb250ZW50LmNvbSIsImtleSI6ImtleTUiLCJleHAiOjE3NzI5OTU0MjgsIm5iZiI6MTc3Mjk5NTEyOCwicGF0aCI6Ii8yNDA5NzEzMjcvNTU5MjIyMTE2LTA1YTFmMjg0LWUwMTAtNDFjNC1hMWFhLTZiNGIyYWIzNzNmMS5qcGc_WC1BbXotQWxnb3JpdGhtPUFXUzQtSE1BQy1TSEEyNTYmWC1BbXotQ3JlZGVudGlhbD1BS0lBVkNPRFlMU0E1M1BRSzRaQSUyRjIwMjYwMzA4JTJGdXMtZWFzdC0xJTJGczMlMkZhd3M0X3JlcXVlc3QmWC1BbXotRGF0ZT0yMDI2MDMwOFQxODM4NDhaJlgtQW16LUV4cGlyZXM9MzAwJlgtQW16LVNpZ25hdHVyZT1lZTVlMTJiNWM4ZTBkNjRjZDNiZWIwODdkYWE1NjFlN2UxOTRhNWFjNGQ2MjE2NjkxZWViMTY4MmUxZGUyNDQ4JlgtQW16LVNpZ25lZEhlYWRlcnM9aG9zdCJ9.vxc0c4NMs5J7CEESs0bzGiJoipdTOYT78BsUHLCX7pw" alt="SliderControl_Schematic" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The KiCad schematic file is at <code>KiCad/Slidercontrol_V2_1_Corrected.kicad_sch</code>.</p>
<p dir="auto">The schematic covers:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Arduino Mega 2560 with all used pin connections</li>
<li>A4988 driver with motor power supply, 100 µF decoupling capacitor and stepper motor</li>
<li>Camera trigger circuit (4N33, R1, 2.5 mm jack)</li>
<li>HC-SR04 ultrasonic sensor (optional, shared pins D47/D49)</li>
<li>TFT shield pin mapping</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Also refer to the pin reference tables in <a href="#3-pin-reference-arduino-mega-2560">Section 3</a> and the circuit diagrams in <a href="#24-camera-trigger-circuit">Section 2.4</a> and <a href="#33-stepper-motor-driver-a4988">Section 3.3</a>.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2. Hardware</h2><a id="user-content-2-hardware" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2. Hardware" href="#2-hardware"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.1 Main Components</h3><a id="user-content-21-main-components" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.1 Main Components" href="#21-main-components"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.2 Hardware History &amp; Incidents</h3><a id="user-content-22-hardware-history--incidents" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.2 Hardware History &amp; Incidents" href="#22-hardware-history--incidents"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">TMC2209 V2.0 - tested, not used in final version</h4><a id="user-content-tmc2209-v20---tested-not-used-in-final-version" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: TMC2209 V2.0 - tested, not used in final version" href="#tmc2209-v20---tested-not-used-in-final-version"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">A test with a TMC2209 V2.0 Ultra Silent 2.5A stepper driver resulted in a cable fire and the burnout of the Arduino Mega's DC-In voltage regulator. The driver was also destroyed in the process. The exact root cause could not be conclusively determined; possible contributing factors include undersized wiring, a pre-existing defect in the DC-In regulator, or an overcurrent condition caused by the driver.</p>
<p dir="auto">Apart from slightly quieter motor operation, the TMC2209 showed no meaningful improvement in motion smoothness compared to the A4988. The stepper motor's planetary gearbox (1:14) already provides inherently smooth and consistent motion, which largely eliminates the benefit of Stealthchop. The final version therefore uses the A4988.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">AZ-Delivery Mega 2560 Clone - replacement after hardware incident</h4><a id="user-content-az-delivery-mega-2560-clone---replacement-after-hardware-incident" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: AZ-Delivery Mega 2560 Clone - replacement after hardware incident" href="#az-delivery-mega-2560-clone---replacement-after-hardware-incident"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Following the failure of the original Arduino Mega 2560, the system runs successfully on an AZ-Delivery Mega 2560 clone. Pin mapping and feature set are fully compatible with the original; all documented functions operate reliably on the clone.</p>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.3 Stepper Motor &amp; Gearbox</h3><a id="user-content-23-stepper-motor--gearbox" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.3 Stepper Motor &amp; Gearbox" href="#23-stepper-motor--gearbox"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The Stepperonline 17HS19-1684s-PG14 features an integrated planetary gearbox with a 1:14 ratio, providing high holding torque at low RPM - well suited for smooth, consistent slider travel. Microstepping is disabled in firmware because the gearbox already provides sufficient mechanical smoothing.</p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Parameter</th>
<th>Value</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Step angle</td>
<td>1.8° (200 full steps/rev)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Gearbox ratio</td>
<td>1:14</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Microstepping</td>
<td>Disabled (pins M1–M3 NC)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Steps/rev in firmware</td>
<td>3200 (200 × 16) - constant retained for reference</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Note:</strong> The 3200 steps/rev constant in the code reflects the full microstepping configuration. With the planetary gearbox and microstepping disabled, effective mechanical resolution differs. The constant is kept for potential use without the gearbox.</p>
</blockquote>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.4 Camera Trigger Circuit</h3><a id="user-content-24-camera-trigger-circuit" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.4 Camera Trigger Circuit" href="#24-camera-trigger-circuit"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The camera trigger provides galvanic isolation between the Arduino and the camera using a 4N33 optocoupler. The Arduino is directly wired into the optocoupler circuit. The optocoupler output is connected via a soldered cable to a <strong>2.5 mm TRS female jack</strong> permanently mounted on the controller housing. From there, a commercially available <strong>2.5 mm male to Canon N3 female adapter cable</strong> connects to the camera.</p>
<p dir="auto">The circuit design follows the approach described by Martyn Currey (<a href="https://www.martyncurrey.com/activating-the-shutter-release/" rel="nofollow">martyncurrey.com/activating-the-shutter-release</a>), adapted for the 4N33 with a 390 Ω input resistor.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Signal Chain</h4><a id="user-content-signal-chain" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Signal Chain" href="#signal-chain"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Arduino D47
    │ (direct wiring)
    ▼

    │ (soldered cable)
    ▼

    │ (commercial cable: 2.5 mm Male → Canon N3 Female)
    ▼
Camera (Canon N3)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Arduino D47
    │ (direct wiring)
    ▼

    │ (soldered cable)
    ▼
2.5 mm TRS Female Jack  ←── permanently mounted on housing
    │ (commercial cable: 2.5 mm Male → Canon N3 Female)
    ▼
Camera (Canon N3)
</code></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">How It Works</h4><a id="user-content-how-it-works" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: How It Works" href="#how-it-works"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The Canon N3 connector places approximately 3.2V on the shutter and focus lines - <strong>this voltage is supplied by the camera itself</strong>, not by the Arduino. Triggering is achieved by <strong>shorting the shutter line to ground</strong> via the optocoupler. The optocoupler ensures there is no electrical connection between the Arduino circuit and the camera circuit, protecting the camera from any voltage on the controller side.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Circuit</h4><a id="user-content-circuit" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Circuit" href="#circuit"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Arduino D47 ──── R1 (390 Ω) ──── 4N33 Pin 1 (Anode)

                                  4N33 Pin 3 (Base) ──── NC
                                  Jack Ring ──── NC         ──[cable]── N3 Focus (not triggered)"><pre class="notranslate"><code>Arduino D47 ──── R1 (390 Ω) ──── 4N33 Pin 1 (Anode)
                                  4N33 Pin 2 (Cathode) ──── Arduino GND

                                  4N33 Pin 4 (Emitter) ──── Jack Sleeve ──[cable]── N3 GND

</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://private-user-images.githubusercontent.com/240971327/559224678-dd89f23e-06e8-402b-b35b-606da665f3c8.jpg?jwt=eyJ0eXAiOiJKV1QiLCJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJpc3MiOiJnaXRodWIuY29tIiwiYXVkIjoicmF3LmdpdGh1YnVzZXJjb250ZW50LmNvbSIsImtleSI6ImtleTUiLCJleHAiOjE3NzI5OTU0MjgsIm5iZiI6MTc3Mjk5NTEyOCwicGF0aCI6Ii8yNDA5NzEzMjcvNTU5MjI0Njc4LWRkODlmMjNlLTA2ZTgtNDAyYi1iMzViLTYwNmRhNjY1ZjNjOC5qcGc_WC1BbXotQWxnb3JpdGhtPUFXUzQtSE1BQy1TSEEyNTYmWC1BbXotQ3JlZGVudGlhbD1BS0lBVkNPRFlMU0E1M1BRSzRaQSUyRjIwMjYwMzA4JTJGdXMtZWFzdC0xJTJGczMlMkZhd3M0X3JlcXVlc3QmWC1BbXotRGF0ZT0yMDI2MDMwOFQxODM4NDhaJlgtQW16LUV4cGlyZXM9MzAwJlgtQW16LVNpZ25hdHVyZT1hNjM0MjA0OWVmNjQ2ZDk1NmY1NGNlMGFiYTZhN2NhNGJlMjM4OWJkODgxMDFiNmJkZWNiYzkzN2IyMDVlNmVhJlgtQW16LVNpZ25lZEhlYWRlcnM9aG9zdCJ9.yAMicsUCYOsBiW5AHvclffRL2445x08cL4aAoboTLLs"><img src="https://private-user-images.githubusercontent.com/240971327/559224678-dd89f23e-06e8-402b-b35b-606da665f3c8.jpg?jwt=eyJ0eXAiOiJKV1QiLCJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJpc3MiOiJnaXRodWIuY29tIiwiYXVkIjoicmF3LmdpdGh1YnVzZXJjb250ZW50LmNvbSIsImtleSI6ImtleTUiLCJleHAiOjE3NzI5OTU0MjgsIm5iZiI6MTc3Mjk5NTEyOCwicGF0aCI6Ii8yNDA5NzEzMjcvNTU5MjI0Njc4LWRkODlmMjNlLTA2ZTgtNDAyYi1iMzViLTYwNmRhNjY1ZjNjOC5qcGc_WC1BbXotQWxnb3JpdGhtPUFXUzQtSE1BQy1TSEEyNTYmWC1BbXotQ3JlZGVudGlhbD1BS0lBVkNPRFlMU0E1M1BRSzRaQSUyRjIwMjYwMzA4JTJGdXMtZWFzdC0xJTJGczMlMkZhd3M0X3JlcXVlc3QmWC1BbXotRGF0ZT0yMDI2MDMwOFQxODM4NDhaJlgtQW16LUV4cGlyZXM9MzAwJlgtQW16LVNpZ25hdHVyZT1hNjM0MjA0OWVmNjQ2ZDk1NmY1NGNlMGFiYTZhN2NhNGJlMjM4OWJkODgxMDFiNmJkZWNiYzkzN2IyMDVlNmVhJlgtQW16LVNpZ25lZEhlYWRlcnM9aG9zdCJ9.yAMicsUCYOsBiW5AHvclffRL2445x08cL4aAoboTLLs" alt="CameraTrigger" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.5 mm TRS Jack Pinout</h4><a id="user-content-25-mm-trs-jack-pinout" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.5 mm TRS Jack Pinout" href="#25-mm-trs-jack-pinout"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Resistor Dimensioning</h4><a id="user-content-resistor-dimensioning" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Resistor Dimensioning" href="#resistor-dimensioning"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<td>60 mA</td>
</tr>

<td>40 mA</td>
</tr>
</tbody>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Trigger Pulse</h4><a id="user-content-trigger-pulse" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Trigger Pulse" href="#trigger-pulse"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Arduino drives <code>TRIGGER_PIN</code> (D47) <code>LOW</code> to close the optocoupler and short the N3 shutter pin to ground, then returns <code>HIGH</code> to release. Pulse duration is configurable in firmware (default: 100 ms).</p>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Note:</strong> Only the shutter contact is triggered. Focus is not connected. For cameras requiring focus + shutter simultaneously (e.g. bulb mode), the focus line would need to be wired in parallel.</p>
</blockquote>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.5 Optional Ultrasonic End-Stop Sensor</h3><a id="user-content-25-optional-ultrasonic-end-stop-sensor" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.5 Optional Ultrasonic End-Stop Sensor" href="#25-optional-ultrasonic-end-stop-sensor"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">An HC-SR04 ultrasonic module can be used as an end-stop safety mechanism. It stops the motor automatically when an obstacle (e.g. the end of the slider rail) is detected within 7 cm. The module shares pins D47 and D49 with the camera trigger - <strong>only one module can be connected at a time.</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">Module detection is automatic at startup: the firmware sends a single ping at maximum range. If a response is received, Sonar Mode is activated (green indicator on display). If the ping fails, Camera Mode is activated (blue indicator).</p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Parameter</th>
<th>Value</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>TRIGGER_PIN</td>
<td>D47 (brown wire)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>ECHO_PIN</td>
<td>D49 (black wire)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>VCC</td>
<td>5V (red wire)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>GND</td>
<td>GND (white wire)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Max. ping distance</td>
<td>200 cm (configurable)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Stop threshold</td>
<td>≤ 7 cm</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Ping interval</td>
<td>50 ms (20× per second)</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<hr>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.6 Controller Housing</h3><a id="user-content-26-controller-housing" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.6 Controller Housing" href="#26-controller-housing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The housing used in early versions of this build is the enclosure published by Marco Kleine-Albers on Thingiverse: <a href="https://www.thingiverse.com/thing:3344179" rel="nofollow">thingiverse.com/thing:3344179</a>. It was printed and used through several beta versions.</p>
<p dir="auto">The original STL files are included in this repository at <code>3D Print/Mega-Testberichte Slider-Case (Arduino Mega+Touch LCD Sainsmart) - 3344179/</code> as an unmodified reference baseline.</p>
<p dir="auto">The housing was later modified to increase internal volume for the additional camera trigger wiring and to improve structural stability through thicker walls. Modified lid files are in <code>3D Print/Drive_Fork/</code>:</p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>File</th>
<th>Description</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><code>deckel_displayseite.v2.stl</code></td>
<td>Modified lid - flat variant, increased wall thickness</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><code>deckel_displayseite.stl</code></td>
<td>Modified lid - raised variant, additional height for cable and electronics volume</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><code>deckel_unterseite.stl</code></td>
<td>Lid underside (modifier body)</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<details>
<summary>Show Photos</summary>summary&gt;
![image (9)](<a href="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/3e00675c-9bf6-42bb-94b2-72b41b06fc5e">https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/3e00675c-9bf6-42bb-94b2-72b41b06fc5e</a>)

</details>
<p dir="auto">Original Housing before raising lid</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">2.7 Motor Drive - Direct Drive vs. Belt Drive</h3><a id="user-content-27-motor-drive---direct-drive-vs-belt-drive" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 2.7 Motor Drive - Direct Drive vs. Belt Drive" href="#27-motor-drive---direct-drive-vs-belt-drive"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Mega-Testberichte.de approach:</strong> The original guide attaches the motor directly to the slider's existing drive belt via a gear adapter, effectively replacing the manual knob with a motor. This removes the ability to operate the slider by hand.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>mein-slider.de housing (used as base here):</strong> The 3D-printed motor housing from mein-slider.de was specifically designed for the iFootage Shark S1 and preserves manual operability by using a separate add-on adapter rather than replacing the original drive belt. However, it routes motor torque through a dedicated secondary drive belt, which created the sourcing problem: no correctly sized belt could be found. The only available belt was too long to tension properly.</p>
<details>
<summary>Show Photos</summary>summary&gt;
![image (1)](<a href="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/7f87cc37-3e26-4848-8b87-030039ecb564">https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/7f87cc37-3e26-4848-8b87-030039ecb564</a>)
![image (2)](<a href="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/4b8538b5-b228-4e78-84f2-9b9a01a2033c">https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/4b8538b5-b228-4e78-84f2-9b9a01a2033c</a>)
![image (3)](<a href="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/746a09bd-04a1-4035-9f70-b4e28effbdca">https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/746a09bd-04a1-4035-9f70-b4e28effbdca</a>)
![image (4)](<a href="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/de8bf87c-e76c-4417-a536-cbc389ef689a">https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/de8bf87c-e76c-4417-a536-cbc389ef689a</a>)
![image](<a href="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/c1c4d273-ce9e-4c24-9468-c92c2bc1083e">https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/c1c4d273-ce9e-4c24-9468-c92c2bc1083e</a>)
</details>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Direct drive solution:</strong> After several experiments scaling the motor housing, a direct drive variant was developed. The motor shaft couples directly to the slider's drive element via a printed adapter, with no belt or intermediate gears.</p>
<p dir="auto">This turned out to be the better solution in every respect:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Full motor torque delivered directly to the slider with no belt slip or stretch</li>
<li>Fewer moving parts means fewer failure points</li>
<li>Smaller and simpler housing</li>
<li>Manual operability of the Shark S1 is retained through the add-on adapter design</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Original drive STL files from the reference design are in <code>3D Print/Original_Drive_STL/</code>.</p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>File</th>
<th>Description</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><code>gehaeuse_unterseite_v2.stl</code></td>
<td>Motor housing - underside</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><code>gehaeuse_motorseite_v02.stl</code></td>
<td>Motor housing - motor-facing side</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><code>antrieb_v02.stl</code></td>
<td>Drive element / motor shaft adapter</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto">The iterative development process - including test prints, fit experiments and the final direct drive solution - is also documented in <code>Fotos_Videos/</code>.</p>
<hr>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Planned Features</h3><a id="user-content-planned-features" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Planned Features" href="#planned-features"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3. Pin Reference (Arduino Mega 2560)</h2><a id="user-content-3-pin-reference-arduino-mega-2560" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3. Pin Reference (Arduino Mega 2560)" href="#3-pin-reference-arduino-mega-2560"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.1 TFT Display</h3><a id="user-content-31-tft-display" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.1 TFT Display" href="#31-tft-display"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The PCB silkscreen uses the prefix <code>LCD_</code> (not <code>TFT_</code>). The signal <code>tft_CD</code> in firmware corresponds to <code>LCD_RS</code> on the board - RS (Register Select) and CD (Command/Data) are the same signal: LOW = command, HIGH = data.</p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Firmware Name</th>
<th>PCB Label</th>
<th>Arduino Mega Pin</th>
<th>Notes</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>tft_CS</td>
<td>LCD_CS</td>
<td>A3</td>
<td>Chip Select</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>tft_CD</td>
<td><strong>LCD_RS</strong></td>
<td>A2</td>
<td>Register Select (= Command/Data)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>tft_WR</td>
<td>LCD_WR</td>
<td>A1</td>
<td>Write</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>tft_RD</td>
<td>LCD_RD</td>
<td>A0</td>
<td>Read</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>tft_RST</td>
<td>LCD_RST</td>
<td>A4</td>
<td>Reset (can also connect to Arduino RST)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>tft_D0 – tft_D1</td>
<td>LCD_D0, LCD_D1</td>
<td>8, 9</td>
<td>8-bit data bus (low bits)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>tft_D2 – tft_D7</td>
<td>LCD_D2 – LCD_D7</td>
<td>2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7</td>
<td>8-bit data bus (high bits)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><em>(not used)</em></td>
<td>SD_SS, SD_DI, SD_DO, SD_SCK</td>
<td>10, 11, 12, 13</td>
<td>SD card interface - not used in this project</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.2 Touchscreen (Resistive)</h3><a id="user-content-32-touchscreen-resistive" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.2 Touchscreen (Resistive)" href="#32-touchscreen-resistive"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.3 Stepper Motor Driver (A4988)</h3><a id="user-content-33-stepper-motor-driver-a4988" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.3 Stepper Motor Driver (A4988)" href="#33-stepper-motor-driver-a4988"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Control Pins (Arduino → A4988)</h4><a id="user-content-control-pins-arduino--a4988" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Control Pins (Arduino → A4988)" href="#control-pins-arduino--a4988"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>

</blockquote>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Ground Separation</h4><a id="user-content-ground-separation" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Ground Separation" href="#ground-separation"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The A4988 has two separate GND pins that must <strong>not</strong> be treated as a single connection:</p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>A4988 GND Pin</th>
<th>Connected to</th>
<th>Carries</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>GND (power side, next to VMOT)</td>
<td>100 µF capacitor (−), then DC jack (−)</td>
<td>Motor current (up to 2A)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>GND (logic side, next to VDD)</td>
<td>Arduino GND</td>
<td>Logic signals only (mA range)</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto">Both grounds share a common reference point at the power supply / DC jack, but should be routed separately on the PCB or in the schematic to avoid mixing high-current motor return paths with logic ground.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Motor Power (PSU → A4988)</h4><a id="user-content-motor-power-psu--a4988" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Motor Power (PSU → A4988)" href="#motor-power-psu--a4988"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>A4988 Pin</th>
<th>Connection</th>
<th>Notes</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>VMOT</td>
<td>12V PSU (+)</td>
<td>Motor supply voltage - 8–35V supported</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>GND (power side)</td>
<td>12V PSU (−)</td>
<td>Motor ground</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto"><strong>100 µF electrolytic capacitor</strong> across VMOT and GND, placed as close to the A4988 as possible. Protects the driver from voltage spikes caused by the motor's inductance.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Motor Coils (A4988 → Stepper)</h4><a id="user-content-motor-coils-a4988--stepper" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Motor Coils (A4988 → Stepper)" href="#motor-coils-a4988--stepper"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>A4988 Pin</th>
<th>Stepper Wire</th>
<th>Coil</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>1A</td>
<td>-</td>
<td>Coil A, terminal 1</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1B</td>
<td>-</td>
<td>Coil A, terminal 2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2A</td>
<td>-</td>
<td>Coil B, terminal 1</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2B</td>
<td>-</td>
<td>Coil B, terminal 2</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto">Coil assignment and wire color depend on the specific motor. For the <strong>17HS19-1684s-PG14</strong> consult the datasheet. Swapping both wires of one coil reverses that coil's polarity and changes rotation direction - equivalent to toggling DIR.</p>
</blockquote>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Current Limit Calibration (VREF)</h4><a id="user-content-current-limit-calibration-vref" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Current Limit Calibration (VREF)" href="#current-limit-calibration-vref"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The A4988 current limit must be set <strong>before connecting the motor</strong>. An incorrectly set current limit risks overheating or damaging the driver and motor.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Required tools:</strong> multimeter, small flathead screwdriver</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Formula (per Pololu):</strong></p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="VREF = I_max x 8 x R_CS"><pre class="notranslate"><code>VREF = I_max x 8 x R_CS
</code></pre></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Variable</th>
<th>Description</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>VREF</td>
<td>Reference voltage to set (measured at potentiometer)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>I_max</td>
<td>Target current limit in amps</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>R_CS</td>
<td>Current sense resistor value on the board</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Determine R_CS first</strong> by inspecting the two small SMD resistors next to the A4988 chip:</p>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Marking</th>
<th>R_CS value</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>R050</td>
<td>0.05 Ohm (original Pololu board)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>R100</td>
<td>0.10 Ohm (most Chinese clones)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>R200</td>
<td>0.20 Ohm</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Measurement procedure:</strong> Connect multimeter negative lead to GND, positive lead to the potentiometer wiper (the metal adjustment screw). Adjust the potentiometer while reading the voltage.</p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Example calculation for the 17HS19-1684s-PG14 (rated 1.68 A):</strong></p>
<p dir="auto">A conservative target of 70% of rated current reduces heat while maintaining reliable torque:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="I_target = 1.68 A x 0.70 = 1.18 A
VREF (R100) = 1.18 x 8 x 0.10 = 0.94 V
VREF (R050) = 1.18 x 8 x 0.05 = 0.47 V"><pre class="notranslate"><code>I_target = 1.68 A x 0.70 = 1.18 A
VREF (R100) = 1.18 x 8 x 0.10 = 0.94 V
VREF (R050) = 1.18 x 8 x 0.05 = 0.47 V
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Per Mega-Testberichte.de, a VREF of <strong>~0.8 V</strong> on an R100 board was found to work well in practice with this motor type, providing reliable torque with acceptable heat generation.</p>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Warning (per Pololu):</strong> Never connect or disconnect the stepper motor while the driver is powered. This can permanently destroy the A4988. Set VREF before attaching the motor, and increase gradually from a low starting value.</p>
</blockquote>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">3.4 Sonar / Camera Trigger (shared)</h3><a id="user-content-34-sonar--camera-trigger-shared" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: 3.4 Sonar / Camera Trigger (shared)" href="#34-sonar--camera-trigger-shared"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<markdown-accessiblity-table><table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Signal</th>
<th>Arduino Mega Pin</th>
<th>Notes</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>TRIGGER_PIN</td>
<td>47</td>
<td>Sonar: trigger output - Camera: shutter pulse (LOW-active)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>ECHO_PIN</td>
<td>49</td>
<td>Sonar: echo input - Camera: not used</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></markdown-accessiblity-table>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><strong>D47 and D49 are shared between the sonar module and the camera trigger.</strong> Automatic detection at startup determines which module is active. Never connect both simultaneously.</p>
</blockquote>

  </div>

</turbo-frame>

    </main>
  </div>
